RT @BeschlossDC: John McCain was released a month after American POWs began coming home 45 years ago today:                        #USN htt‚Ä¶
On February 28, by a two-vote majority, the Senate denied Gallatin his seat. This open-door experiment prompted the Senate to permanently open its proceedings once a public gallery had been built. (3/3)
Albert Gallatin had already had taken his oath, but sens questioned whether the Swiss-born senator had been a US citizen for the constitutionally required 9 years. To avoid criticism, senators determined on Feb 11, 1794, that the case should be resolved in full public view. (2/3)
This week in Senate history, courtesy of https://t.co/V6bu1eemSU.	Meeting at Congress Hall in Philadelphia, the Senate temporarily abandoned its practice of conducting business behind closed doors while it considered whether or not to seat one of Pennsylvania's senators. (1/3)

The Senate Republican tax overhaul (H.R. 1) passed by a vote of 51 to 49. Republican Corker voted NAY.
The Senate is about to vote on passage of H.R. 1, the legislative vehicle for the Senate Republican tax package.
By a vote of 52 to 48, the Senate passed Merkley amendment to strike the Hillsdale College tax benefit from the bill. Republicans voting YEA: Collins, Fischer, Kennedy and Murkowski.
Cantwell amendment to forbid oil drilling in the Alaska National Wildlife Refuge failed to get a budget waiver, by a vote of 48 to 52. Republican Collins voted YEA. Democrat Manchin voted NAY. Vote was otherwise party-line.
By a vote of 38 to 61, the Manchin motion to commit failed.
By a vote of 34 to 65, the budget waiver failed for the Kaine amendment (#1846, middle class tax cuts). NAYS: all Republicans, 12 Democrats and independent Sanders.
Republicans Collins and Murkowski voted NAY on the Cruz amendment, making Pence's vote necessary to break the 50 to 50 tie.
Pence breaks the tie. Cruz amendment on education savings plans passes 51 to 50.
